## Chapter 20: Public Participation in Planning:




### Introduction

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial aspects of modern planning practice. As our world becomes increasingly complex and interconnected, the potential for disasters and crises is ever-present. These events can have devastating impacts on communities, economies, and the environment. Therefore, it is essential for planners to have a comprehensive understanding of disaster planning and resilience in order to effectively mitigate and respond to these events.

In this chapter, we will explore the concept of disaster planning and resilience, and its importance in the field of planning. We will discuss the various types of disasters and crises that can occur, and the different approaches and strategies that can be used to plan for and respond to them. We will also delve into the role of planners in disaster planning and resilience, and the skills and knowledge that are necessary for this important work.

Through this chapter, we aim to provide a comprehensive overview of disaster planning and resilience, and to equip readers with the necessary knowledge and tools to effectively address these critical issues in their own planning practice. By understanding the complexities of disaster planning and resilience, planners can play a crucial role in creating more resilient and sustainable communities that are better equipped to handle the challenges of the future.




### Section: 20.1 Importance of Disaster Planning:

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial aspects of modern planning practice. As our world becomes increasingly complex and interconnected, the potential for disasters and crises is ever-present. These events can have devastating impacts on communities, economies, and the environment. Therefore, it is essential for planners to have a comprehensive understanding of disaster planning and resilience in order to effectively mitigate and respond to these events.

#### 20.1a Role in Urban Planning

Urban planning plays a critical role in disaster planning and resilience. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they become more vulnerable to disasters and crises. Therefore, it is the responsibility of urban planners to incorporate disaster planning and resilience into their overall planning strategies.

One of the key ways in which urban planning contributes to disaster planning and resilience is through the consideration of urban climatology. Urban climatology is the study of the impact of the urban environment on weather and climate. It is a crucial aspect of urban planning as it helps planners make informed decisions about pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater modeling. By understanding the effects of urban climatology, planners can design and implement strategies that mitigate the potential impacts of disasters and crises.

Another important aspect of urban planning in disaster planning and resilience is regional planning. Regional planning deals with the planning of land use, infrastructure, and settlement growth over a geographical area that extends beyond a single city. This type of planning is essential in disaster planning as it allows for a more comprehensive and coordinated approach to disaster preparedness and response. By considering the needs and vulnerabilities of the entire region, planners can develop more effective disaster plans and increase overall resilience.

Urban planning also plays a crucial role in heritage and conservation efforts. As cities continue to grow and develop, there is a risk of losing important cultural heritage sites and buildings. Urban planners are responsible for identifying, protecting, and conserving these sites and buildings. This includes developing plans and policies that promote the preservation of cultural heritage while also considering the potential impacts of disasters and crises.

In addition to these specific roles, urban planning also plays a general role in disaster planning and resilience. By considering the overall design and layout of a city, planners can incorporate disaster planning and resilience into every aspect of urban development. This includes incorporating green spaces and natural infrastructure, promoting sustainable building practices, and developing emergency response plans.

In conclusion, urban planning is a crucial aspect of disaster planning and resilience. By incorporating disaster planning and resilience into all aspects of urban development, planners can help mitigate the impacts of disasters and crises and create more resilient and sustainable cities. 





### Section: 20.1 Importance of Disaster Planning:

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial aspects of modern planning practice. As our world becomes increasingly complex and interconnected, the potential for disasters and crises is ever-present. These events can have devastating impacts on communities, economies, and the environment. Therefore, it is essential for planners to have a comprehensive understanding of disaster planning and resilience in order to effectively mitigate and respond to these events.

#### 20.1a Role in Urban Planning

Urban planning plays a critical role in disaster planning and resilience. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they become more vulnerable to disasters and crises. Therefore, it is the responsibility of urban planners to incorporate disaster planning and resilience into their overall planning strategies.

One of the key ways in which urban planning contributes to disaster planning and resilience is through the consideration of urban climatology. Urban climatology is the study of the impact of the urban environment on weather and climate. It is a crucial aspect of urban planning as it helps planners make informed decisions about pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater modeling. By understanding the effects of urban climatology, planners can design and implement strategies that mitigate the potential impacts of disasters and crises.

Another important aspect of urban planning in disaster planning and resilience is regional planning. Regional planning deals with the planning of land use, infrastructure, and settlement growth over a geographical area that extends beyond a single city. This type of planning is essential in disaster planning as it allows for a more comprehensive and coordinated approach to disaster preparedness and response. By considering the needs and vulnerabilities of the entire region, planners can develop more effective disaster plans and increase overall resilience.

Urban planning also plays a crucial role in disaster planning and resilience through the implementation of disaster-resilient design. This approach involves incorporating disaster-resilient features into the design of buildings, infrastructure, and urban spaces. These features can help mitigate the impacts of disasters and crises, and aid in the recovery process. For example, incorporating green infrastructure, such as green roofs and rain gardens, can help reduce the impact of flooding and improve air quality. Additionally, designing buildings to withstand extreme weather events, such as hurricanes and earthquakes, can help minimize damage and disruption.

#### 20.1b Impact on Communities

Disasters and crises have a significant impact on communities, both in terms of physical damage and social disruption. The loss of homes, businesses, and infrastructure can have a devastating effect on the livelihoods and well-being of individuals and families. Additionally, the loss of community cohesion and social support can exacerbate the impacts of a disaster.

Disaster planning and resilience efforts aim to mitigate these impacts and help communities recover more quickly. By incorporating disaster-resilient design and implementing effective disaster plans, planners can help minimize the damage and disruption caused by disasters and crises. This not only helps protect the physical infrastructure of a community, but also helps preserve the social fabric and sense of community that is so important in times of crisis.

#### 20.1c Case Studies

To further illustrate the importance of disaster planning and resilience, let's examine two case studies: the 2017 hurricane season in the United States and the 2010 earthquake in Haiti.

The 2017 hurricane season in the United States was one of the most destructive on record, with three Category 4 hurricanes making landfall in the country. These hurricanes caused widespread damage to infrastructure, homes, and businesses, and resulted in significant loss of life. However, due to the implementation of disaster planning and resilience efforts, the impacts of these hurricanes were mitigated. For example, in Houston, Texas, the implementation of green infrastructure, such as green roofs and rain gardens, helped reduce the impact of flooding from Hurricane Harvey. Additionally, the use of disaster-resilient design in buildings and infrastructure helped minimize damage and aid in the recovery process.

The 2010 earthquake in Haiti was a devastating event that caused widespread destruction and loss of life. The lack of disaster planning and resilience efforts in the country resulted in a slow and difficult recovery process. However, the implementation of disaster planning and resilience efforts in neighboring Dominican Republic, which shares the same island as Haiti, resulted in a more efficient and effective response to the earthquake. This highlights the importance of incorporating disaster planning and resilience into overall planning strategies, especially in vulnerable communities.

In conclusion, disaster planning and resilience are crucial aspects of modern planning practice. By considering urban climatology, regional planning, and disaster-resilient design, planners can help mitigate the impacts of disasters and crises and aid in the recovery process. These efforts not only protect the physical infrastructure of a community, but also preserve the social fabric and sense of community that is so important in times of crisis. 





### Section: 20.1 Importance of Disaster Planning:

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial aspects of modern planning practice. As our world becomes increasingly complex and interconnected, the potential for disasters and crises is ever-present. These events can have devastating impacts on communities, economies, and the environment. Therefore, it is essential for planners to have a comprehensive understanding of disaster planning and resilience in order to effectively mitigate and respond to these events.

#### 20.1a Role in Urban Planning

Urban planning plays a critical role in disaster planning and resilience. As cities continue to grow and evolve, they become more vulnerable to disasters and crises. Therefore, it is the responsibility of urban planners to incorporate disaster planning and resilience into their overall planning strategies.

One of the key ways in which urban planning contributes to disaster planning and resilience is through the consideration of urban climatology. Urban climatology is the study of the impact of the urban environment on weather and climate. It is a crucial aspect of urban planning as it helps planners make informed decisions about pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater modeling. By understanding the effects of urban climatology, planners can design and implement strategies that mitigate the potential impacts of disasters and crises.

Another important aspect of urban planning in disaster planning and resilience is regional planning. Regional planning deals with the planning of land use, infrastructure, and settlement growth over a geographical area that extends beyond a single city. This type of planning is essential in disaster planning as it allows for a more comprehensive and coordinated approach to disaster preparedness and response. By considering the needs and vulnerabilities of the entire region, planners can develop more effective disaster plans and increase overall resilience.

Urban planning also plays a crucial role in disaster planning and resilience through the incorporation of disaster-resilient design principles. These principles aim to minimize the impact of disasters on a community by considering the potential risks and vulnerabilities in the design and construction of buildings, infrastructure, and urban spaces. By incorporating disaster-resilient design principles, urban planners can help communities better withstand and recover from disasters.

#### 20.1b Importance of Disaster Planning in Urban Development

Disaster planning is essential in urban development as it helps mitigate the potential impacts of disasters on a community. By considering the potential risks and vulnerabilities in the planning and design of urban spaces, planners can develop strategies that minimize the impact of disasters and increase the resilience of a community.

One of the key ways in which disaster planning is important in urban development is through the consideration of disaster-resilient design principles. These principles aim to minimize the impact of disasters on a community by incorporating disaster-resilient design features into the design and construction of buildings, infrastructure, and urban spaces. By incorporating these principles, urban planners can help communities better withstand and recover from disasters.

Another important aspect of disaster planning in urban development is the consideration of disaster-resilient infrastructure. This includes the design and construction of infrastructure that can withstand and recover from disasters, such as earthquake-resistant buildings, flood-resistant roads, and disaster-resistant power grids. By incorporating disaster-resilient infrastructure, urban planners can help minimize the impact of disasters on a community and increase overall resilience.

Disaster planning is also crucial in urban development as it allows for a more comprehensive and coordinated approach to disaster preparedness and response. By considering the needs and vulnerabilities of the entire community, urban planners can develop more effective disaster plans and increase overall resilience. This is especially important in today's interconnected world, where disasters can have far-reaching impacts on multiple communities.

In conclusion, disaster planning is a crucial aspect of urban development. By incorporating disaster-resilient design principles, disaster-resilient infrastructure, and a comprehensive approach to disaster preparedness and response, urban planners can help communities better withstand and recover from disasters. This is essential in today's complex and interconnected world, where the potential for disasters and crises is ever-present. 





### Section: 20.2 Strategies for Building Resilience:

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial for mitigating the impacts of disasters and crises. In this section, we will explore various strategies that can be used to build resilience in the face of disasters and crises.

#### 20.2a Climate Change Adaptation

Climate change is a major factor that can exacerbate the impacts of disasters and crises. As the Earth's climate continues to change, it is essential for planners to consider the potential effects of climate change on their disaster planning and resilience strategies.

One strategy for building resilience in the face of climate change is through adaptation. Adaptation involves making changes to systems and processes in order to better cope with the impacts of climate change. This can include incorporating climate change considerations into disaster planning, as well as implementing measures to reduce vulnerability to climate change impacts.

One example of adaptation is the development of crop varieties with greater drought tolerance. As climate change alters rainfall patterns and increases evaporation, this can have a significant impact on agriculture. By developing drought-tolerant crops, farmers can reduce their vulnerability to drought and increase their resilience in the face of climate change.

Another adaptation strategy is the use of local rainwater storage. In areas where water availability is a concern, such as in semi-arid regions, the use of small planting basins can help harvest water and boost crop yields. This can be particularly beneficial in areas where rainfall is scarce, as it can help mitigate the impacts of drought.

In addition to these adaptation strategies, it is also important for planners to consider the potential impacts of climate change on other aspects of disaster planning and resilience. For example, as sea levels rise and extreme weather events become more frequent, coastal communities may need to consider relocation or fortification of infrastructure. Similarly, as temperatures rise, the risk of wildfires and other natural disasters may increase, requiring additional adaptation measures.

Overall, climate change adaptation is a crucial aspect of building resilience in the face of disasters and crises. By incorporating climate change considerations into disaster planning and implementing adaptation strategies, we can better prepare for and mitigate the impacts of climate change on our communities.


#### 20.2b Community Engagement

Community engagement is a crucial aspect of building resilience in the face of disasters and crises. It involves actively involving community members in the planning and implementation of disaster planning and resilience strategies. This not only helps to ensure that the strategies are effective and appropriate for the community, but also helps to build trust and ownership among community members.

One way to engage the community is through the use of social media. Social media platforms, such as Twitter and Facebook, can be used to disseminate information and gather feedback from community members. This can be particularly useful in the aftermath of a disaster, when traditional communication channels may be disrupted. By using social media, community members can quickly access important information and provide feedback on the disaster response.

Another way to engage the community is through the use of community-based participatory research (CBPR). CBPR involves actively involving community members in the research process, from identifying research questions to collecting and analyzing data. This approach not only helps to ensure that the research is relevant and meaningful to the community, but also helps to build trust and ownership among community members.

In addition to these specific strategies, it is important for planners to consider the overall approach to community engagement. This includes being transparent and honest in communication, actively listening to community concerns and feedback, and involving community members in decision-making processes. By actively engaging the community, planners can help to build resilience and ensure that disaster planning and response strategies are effective and appropriate for the community.


#### 20.2c Case Studies in Resilience

In this section, we will explore some case studies that demonstrate successful strategies for building resilience in the face of disasters and crises. These case studies will provide real-world examples and insights into how different communities have effectively implemented disaster planning and resilience strategies.

One such case study is the city of Mayantoc in the Philippines. Mayantoc has implemented a comprehensive disaster management plan that includes community-based disaster risk reduction (CBDRR) and climate change adaptation. The city has also established a disaster risk reduction and management council, which includes representatives from various sectors such as government, non-governmental organizations, and community groups. This council works together to develop and implement disaster management plans and policies.

In terms of CBDRR, Mayantoc has implemented a participatory approach that involves community members in the planning and implementation of disaster risk reduction strategies. This has helped to build trust and ownership among community members, and has also ensured that the strategies are effective and appropriate for the community. Additionally, the city has incorporated climate change adaptation measures, such as the use of local rainwater storage and the development of drought-tolerant crops, to mitigate the impacts of climate change on the community.

Another successful case study is the city of Copenhagen in Denmark. Copenhagen has implemented a sustainable urban development strategy that includes disaster planning and resilience measures. The city has prioritized the use of green infrastructure, such as green roofs and rain gardens, to mitigate the impacts of extreme weather events and climate change. Additionally, Copenhagen has implemented a comprehensive disaster management plan that includes evacuation routes, emergency shelters, and communication systems.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of a comprehensive and community-based approach to disaster planning and resilience. By actively involving community members in the planning and implementation of strategies, and by considering the overall approach to community engagement, these communities have been able to effectively build resilience in the face of disasters and crises. These case studies can serve as valuable examples for other communities looking to implement similar strategies.





### Section: 20.2 Strategies for Building Resilience:

Disaster planning and resilience are crucial for mitigating the impacts of disasters and crises. In this section, we will explore various strategies that can be used to build resilience in the face of disasters and crises.

#### 20.2b Community Resilience

Community resilience is a crucial aspect of disaster planning and resilience. It involves building the ability of a community to withstand and recover from disasters and crises. This can include both physical and social resilience, as well as the ability to adapt and thrive in the face of challenges.

One strategy for building community resilience is through community-based disaster risk management (CBDRM). This approach involves engaging the community in the planning and implementation of disaster risk management strategies. By involving the community, CBDRM can help build a sense of ownership and responsibility for disaster planning and resilience.

Another strategy for building community resilience is through community-based disaster risk reduction (CBDRR). This approach focuses on reducing the risk of disasters and crises through community-led initiatives. This can include measures such as disaster risk assessments, early warning systems, and disaster preparedness training.

In addition to these strategies, it is also important to consider the role of community resilience in the face of climate change. As the impacts of climate change continue to worsen, it is essential for communities to have the ability to adapt and thrive in the face of these challenges. This can include incorporating climate change considerations into disaster planning, as well as implementing measures to reduce vulnerability to climate change impacts.

One example of building community resilience in the face of climate change is through the development of community-based adaptation (CBA) strategies. These strategies involve engaging communities in the planning and implementation of adaptation measures, such as building more resilient infrastructure and implementing sustainable practices. By involving the community, CBA can help build a sense of ownership and responsibility for adaptation, as well as increase the effectiveness of adaptation efforts.

Another example is through the use of community-based disaster risk financing (CBDRF). This approach involves using financial instruments, such as insurance or microfinance, to help communities mitigate and recover from disasters and crises. By providing financial resources, CBDRF can help communities build resilience and reduce the impacts of disasters and crises.

In conclusion, community resilience is a crucial aspect of disaster planning and resilience. By involving the community in disaster planning and implementing strategies such as CBDRM, CBDRR, and CBA, we can build a more resilient and adaptive community that is better equipped to face the challenges of disasters and crises. 





### Subsection: 20.2c Case Studies

In this subsection, we will explore some real-world case studies that demonstrate the strategies for building resilience discussed in the previous section.

#### 20.2c.1 Community-Based Disaster Risk Management in the Philippines

The Philippines is one of the most disaster-prone countries in the world, experiencing an average of 20 typhoons per year. In 2013, the country was hit by Super Typhoon Haiyan, which caused widespread destruction and loss of life. In response to this disaster, the community of Guiuan in Eastern Samar implemented a community-based disaster risk management (CBDRM) approach.

The community engaged in a participatory process to identify and prioritize disaster risks and develop a disaster risk management plan. This included conducting a disaster risk assessment, establishing an early warning system, and training community members in disaster preparedness and response. As a result of these efforts, the community was able to mitigate the impacts of Typhoon Haiyan and reduce the number of casualties.

#### 20.2c.2 Community-Based Disaster Risk Reduction in Bangladesh

Bangladesh is also a highly disaster-prone country, with frequent floods and cyclones. In 2007, the country experienced Cyclone Sidr, which caused significant damage and loss of life. In response to this disaster, the community of Khulna implemented a community-based disaster risk reduction (CBDRR) approach.

The community engaged in a participatory process to identify and prioritize disaster risks and develop a disaster risk reduction plan. This included conducting a disaster risk assessment, establishing an early warning system, and implementing measures to reduce vulnerability to future disasters. As a result of these efforts, the community was able to reduce the impacts of Cyclone Sidr and increase their resilience to future disasters.

#### 20.2c.3 Community-Based Adaptation in Small Island Developing States

Small Island Developing States (SIDS) are particularly vulnerable to the impacts of climate change, including sea level rise, coastal erosion, and extreme weather events. In response to these challenges, the community of Tuvalu implemented a community-based adaptation (CBA) strategy.

The community engaged in a participatory process to identify and prioritize climate change risks and develop an adaptation plan. This included conducting a climate risk assessment, establishing an early warning system, and implementing measures to reduce vulnerability to climate change impacts. As a result of these efforts, the community was able to increase their resilience to the impacts of climate change and adapt to the changing climate.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the effectiveness of various strategies for building resilience in the face of disasters and crises. By engaging the community in the planning and implementation of disaster risk management and reduction strategies, we can increase their ability to withstand and recover from disasters and crises. Additionally, incorporating climate change considerations into disaster planning and implementing community-based adaptation strategies can help communities adapt and thrive in the face of climate change impacts.
